Note that the choice of `ddof` is unlikely to\n855:     affect model performance.\n856: \n857:     Examples\n858:     --------\n859:     >>> from sklearn.preprocessing import StandardScaler\n860:     >>> data = [[0, 0], [0, 0], [1, 1], [1, 1]]\n861:     >>> scaler = StandardScaler()\n862:     >>> print(scaler.fit(data))\n863:     StandardScaler()\n864:     >>> print(scaler.mean_)\n865:     [0.5 0.5]\n866:     >>> print(scaler.transform(data))\n867:     [[-1. -1.]\n868:      [-1. -1.]\n869:      [ 1.  1.]\n870:      [ 1.  1.]]\n871:     >>> print(scaler.transform([[2, 2]]))\n872:     [[3. 3.]]\n873:     \"\"\"\n874: \n875:     _parameter_constraints: dict = {\n876:         \"copy\": [\"boolean\"],\n877:         \"with_mean\": [\"boolean\"],\n878:         \"with_std\": [\"boolean\"],\n879:     }\n880: \n881:     def __init__(self, *, copy=True, with_mean=True, with_std=True):\n882:         self.with_mean = with_mean\n883:         self.with_std = with_std\n884:         self.copy = copy\n885: \n886:     def _reset(self):\n887:         \"\"\"Reset internal data-dependent state of the scaler, if necessary.\n888: \n889:         __init__ parameters are not touched.\n890:         \"\"\"\n891:         # Checking one attribute is enough, because they are all set together\n892:         # in partial_fit\n893:         if hasattr(self, \"scale_\"):\n894:             del self.scale_\n895:             del self.n_samples_seen_\n896:             del self.mean_\n897:             del self.var_\n898: \n899:     def fit(self, X, y=None, sample_weight=None):\n900:         \"\"\"Compute the mean and std to be used for later scaling.\n901: \n902:         Parameters\n903:         ----------\n904:         X : {array-like, sparse matrix} of shape (n_samples, n_features)\n905:             The data used to compute the mean and standard deviation\n906:             used for later scaling along the features axis.\n907: \n908:         y : None\n909:             Ignored.\n910: \n911:         sample_weight : array-like of shape (n_samples,), default=None\n912:             Individual weights for each sample.\n913: \n914:             .. versionadded:: 0.24\n915:                parameter *sample_weight* support to StandardScaler.\n916: \n917:         Returns\n918:         -------\n919:         self : object\n920:             Fitted scaler.\n921:         \"\"\"\n922:         # Reset internal state before fitting\n923:         self._reset()\n924:         return self.partial_fit(X, y, sample_weight)\n925: \n926:     @_fit_context(prefer_skip_nested_validation=True)\n927:     def partial_fit(self, X, y=None, sample_weight=None):\n928:         \"\"\"Online computation of mean and std on X for later scaling.\n929: \n930:         All of X is processed as a single batch. This is intended for cases\n931:         when :meth:`fit` is not feasible due to very large number of\n932:         `n_samples` or because X is read from a continuous stream.\n933: \n934:         The algorithm for incremental mean and std is given in Equation 1.5a,b\n935:         in Chan, Tony F., Gene H. Golub, and Randall J. LeVeque. \"Algorithms\n936:         for computing the sample variance: Analysis and recommendations.\"\n937:         The American Statistician 37.3 (1983): 242-247:\n938: \n939:         Parameters\n940:         ----------\n941:         X : {array-like, sparse matrix} of shape (n_samples, n_features)\n942:             The data used to compute the mean and standard deviation\n943:             used for later scaling along the features axis.\n944: \n945:         y : None\n946:             Ignored.\n947: \n948:         sample_weight : array-like of shape (n_samples,), default=None\n949:             Individual weights for each sample.\n950: \n951: ","url":"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/scikit-learn--cb7e82dd@72904752e88f414cbc543dac5945b6c8dd7b34fa/-/blob/sklearn/preprocessing/_data.py%3FL800-950"}}}

Entry Point: scikit-learn preprocessing (sklearn/preprocessing/_data.py)\n\n**File**: `sklearn/preprocessing/_data.py:961`\n**Function**: `StandardScaler.partial_fit()`\n\n```python\nX = validate_data(\n    self,\n    X,\n    accept_sparse=(\"csr\", \"csc\"),\n    dtype=supported_float_dtypes(xp, X_device),\n    ensure_all_finite=\"allow-nan\",\n    reset=first_call,\n)\n```\n\nThe `validate_data()` function is called to prepare input data for processing. The `dtype` parameter is set to `supported_float_dtypes()` which includes `np.float64` and `np.float32`.\n\n### 2. Input Validation: scikit-learn utils (sklearn/utils/validation.py)\n\n**File**: `sklearn/utils/validation.py:2912`\n**Function**: `validate_data()`\n\n```python\nout = check_array(X, input_name=\"X\", **check_params)\n```\n\n`validate_data()` delegates to `check_array()` to perform the actual validation and dtype conversion.\n\n### 3. Array Checking: scikit-learn validation (sklearn/utils/validation.py)\n\n**File**: `sklearn/utils/validation.py:1022`\n**Function**: `check_array()`\n\n```python\narray = _asarray_with_order(array, order=order, dtype=dtype, xp=xp)\n```\n\nWhen `check_array()` encounters a pandas DataFrame or Series with extension dtypes like `Int64Dtype`, it calls `_asarray_with_order()` to convert it to a NumPy array with the requested dtype (float64).\n\n### 4. NumPy Conversion Wrapper (sklearn/utils/_array_api.py)\n\n**File**: `sklearn/utils/_array_api.py:910`\n**Function**: `_asarray_with_order()`\n\n```python\nif copy is True:\n    array = numpy.array(array, order=order, dtype=dtype)\nelse:\n    array = numpy.asarray(array, order=order, dtype=dtype)\n```\n\nSince `copy` is not explicitly set (defaults to `None`), line 910 is executed, calling `numpy.asarray()` with `dtype=float64` and no explicit `copy` parameter.\n\n### 5. NumPy Array Interface Protocol\n\nWhen `numpy.asarray()` is called on a pandas nullable integer array, NumPy uses the `__array__` protocol to get the array data. This calls the object's `__array__` method if it exists.\n\n### 6. Pandas Nullable Integer Conversion: ROOT CAUSE (pandas/core/arrays/masked.py)\n\n**File**: `pandas/core/arrays/masked.py:694-716`\n**Function**: `BaseMaskedArray.__array__()`\n\n```python\ndef __array__(\n    self, dtype: NpDtype | None = None, copy: bool | None = None\n) -> np.ndarray:\n    \"\"\"\n    the array interface, return my values\n    We return an object array here to preserve our scalar values\n    \"\"\"\n    if copy is False:\n        if not self._hasna:\n            # special case, here we can simply return the underlying data\n            result = np.array(self._data, dtype=dtype, copy=copy)\n            # If the ExtensionArray is readonly, make the numpy array readonly too\n            if self._readonly:\n                result = result.view()\n                result.flags.writeable = False\n            return result\n        raise ValueError(\n            \"Unable to avoid copy while creating an array as requested.\"\n        )\n\n    if copy is None:\n        copy = False  # The NumPy copy=False meaning is different here.\n    return self.to_numpy(dtype=dtype, copy=copy)\n```\n\n### Root Cause Details\n\nThe incompatibility occurs at **lines 701-712** in `pandas/core/arrays/masked.py`:\n\n**Problem**: When `numpy.asarray()` calls `__array__()` with the default behavior (no explicit copy parameter), NumPy doesn't pass the `copy` parameter to `__array__()`, which means `copy=False` by default.\n\nWhen:\n1. `copy=False` is passed\n2. AND the masked array has missing values (`self._hasna = True`)\n3. The method raises `ValueError(\"Unable to avoid copy while creating an array as requested.\")`\n\nThis happens because:\n- **Line 701-702**: Checks if `copy is False` and `self._hasna` (has missing values)\n- **Line 710-712**: If both conditions are true, raises a `ValueError`\n\nThe logic here is: pandas refuses to convert the array without making a copy when there are missing values, because:\n1. Converting Int64 with NA to float64 requires replacing NA values with NaN\n2. This requires modifying the data, which is a copy operation\n3. When `copy=False`, pandas cannot fulfill this request\n\n## Impact\n\n**Affected Components**:\n- `sklearn.preprocessing.StandardScaler`\n- `sklearn.preprocessing.MinMaxScaler`\n- Any other sklearn preprocessing that uses `check_array()` with float dtypes\n\n**Affected Inputs**:\n- pandas DataFrames with nullable integer columns containing missing values\n- pandas Series with `Int8Dtype`, `Int16Dtype`, `Int32Dtype`, `Int64Dtype`, `UInt8Dtype`, `UInt16Dtype`, `UInt32Dtype`, `UInt64Dtype`\n\n**Symptom**:\n```\nValueError: Unable to avoid copy while creating an array as requested.\n```\n\n## Root Cause Summary\n\n| Component | File | Line | Issue |\n|-----------|------|------|-------|\n| **pandas (Root Cause)** | `pandas/core/arrays/masked.py` | **694-716** | `__array__()` raises error when `copy=False` and array has missing values |\n| pandas | `pandas/core/arrays/masked.py` | 512-606 | `to_numpy()` properly handles conversion but requires copy |\n| sklearn | `sklearn/utils/_array_api.py` | 910 | Calls `numpy.asarray()` without explicit `copy=True` |\n| sklearn | `sklearn/utils/validation.py` | 1022 | `check_array()` uses `_asarray_with_order()` for dtype conversion |\n| scikit-learn | `sklearn/preprocessing/_data.py` | 961 | `partial_fit()` calls `validate_data()` expecting NumPy array |\n\n## Exact Location of Root Cause\n\n**File**: `pandas/core/arrays/masked.py`\n**Lines**: 701-712\n**Method**: `BaseMaskedArray.__array__()`\n\n```python\n701:    if copy is False:\n702:        if not self._hasna:\n703:            # special case, here we can simply return the underlying data\n704:            result = np.array(self._data, dtype=dtype, copy=copy)\n705:            # If the ExtensionArray is readonly, make the numpy array readonly too\n706:            if self._readonly:\n707:                result = result.view()\n708:                result.flags.writeable = False\n709:            return result\n710:        raise ValueError(\n711:            \"Unable to avoid copy while creating an array as requested.\"\n712:        )\n```\n\n## Why It's a Problem\n\n1. **Incompatible Default Behavior**: When NumPy's `asarray()` calls `__array__()`, it doesn't explicitly pass `copy=True`, leaving it as `None` or using NumPy's default semantics.\n\n2. **Data Loss Risk**: The pandas design prevents implicit copies to protect data integrity, but this creates a barrier for users who want to use modern nullable dtypes with sklearn.\n\n3. **Incomplete Dtype Conversion**: While `to_numpy()` (called on line 716) can properly convert with a copy, the early exit condition on line 710-712 prevents this from being reached when `copy=False`.\n\n## Solution Approach\n\nThe issue needs to be resolved at the sklearn integration level by explicitly requesting a copy when needed, or pandas could adjust the `__array__` protocol handling for better numpy compatibility.\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":10,"cache_creation_input_tokens":2003,"cache_read_input_tokens":97582,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":2003},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"dbf9dd60-386b-48ff-bbd9-b193a8ca4108","uuid":"988b3b8f-33f1-4c74-bac8-1124ab4f1da1"}

Array Checking: scikit-learn validation (sklearn/utils/validation.py)\n\n**File**: `sklearn/utils/validation.py:1022`\n**Function**: `check_array()`\n\n```python\narray = _asarray_with_order(array, order=order, dtype=dtype, xp=xp)\n```\n\nWhen `check_array()` encounters a pandas DataFrame or Series with extension dtypes like `Int64Dtype`, it calls `_asarray_with_order()` to convert it to a NumPy array with the requested dtype (float64).\n\n### 4. AND the masked array has missing values (`self._hasna = True`)\n3. The method raises `ValueError(\"Unable to avoid copy while creating an array as requested.\")`\n\nThis happens because:\n- **Line 701-702**: Checks if `copy is False` and `self._hasna` (has missing values)\n- **Line 710-712**: If both conditions are true, raises a `ValueError`\n\nThe logic here is: pandas refuses to convert the array without making a copy when there are missing values, because:\n1. Converting Int64 with NA to float64 requires replacing NA values with NaN\n2. This requires modifying the data, which is a copy operation\n3. When `copy=False`, pandas cannot fulfill this request\n\n## Impact\n\n**Affected Components**:\n- `sklearn.preprocessing.StandardScaler`\n- `sklearn.preprocessing.MinMaxScaler`\n- Any other sklearn preprocessing that uses `check_array()` with float dtypes\n\n**Affected Inputs**:\n- pandas DataFrames with nullable integer columns containing missing values\n- pandas Series with `Int8Dtype`, `Int16Dtype`, `Int32Dtype`, `Int64Dtype`, `UInt8Dtype`, `UInt16Dtype`, `UInt32Dtype`, `UInt64Dtype`\n\n**Symptom**:\n```\nValueError: Unable to avoid copy while creating an array as requested.\n```\n\n## Root Cause Summary\n\n| Component | File | Line | Issue |\n|-----------|------|------|-------|\n| **pandas (Root Cause)** | `pandas/core/arrays/masked.py` | **694-716** | `__array__()` raises error when `copy=False` and array has missing values |\n| pandas | `pandas/core/arrays/masked.py` | 512-606 | `to_numpy()` properly handles conversion but requires copy |\n| sklearn | `sklearn/utils/_array_api.py` | 910 | Calls `numpy.asarray()` without explicit `copy=True` |\n| sklearn | `sklearn/utils/validation.py` | 1022 | `check_array()` uses `_asarray_with_order()` for dtype conversion |\n| scikit-learn | `sklearn/preprocessing/_data.py` | 961 | `partial_fit()` calls `validate_data()` expecting NumPy array |\n\n## Exact Location of Root Cause\n\n**File**: `pandas/core/arrays/masked.py`\n**Lines**: 701-712\n**Method**: `BaseMaskedArray.__array__()`\n\n```python\n701:    if copy is False:\n702:        if not self._hasna:\n703:            #
